# GluN1-GluN2B NMDA Receptor (Xenopus laevis, Full-Length)

## Overview

The full-length N-methyl-[D Aspartate](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/substrates/l-aspartate/) (NMDA) receptor composed of GluN1 and GluN2B subunits from Xenopus laevis, solved by X-ray crystallography and cryo-EM. NMDA receptors are ligand-gated ion channels that serve as coincidence detectors in excitatory synaptic transmission, requiring both glycine and glutamate binding plus membrane depolarization to relieve voltage-dependent magnesium block. X-ray structures reveal the closed-blocked channel state with mushroom-like architecture. Cryo-EM structures at resolutions of 5.0-6.8 Angstroms reveal three distinct conformational states (active, non-active1, non-active2) captured in the presence of glycine and [L Glutamate](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/substrates/l-glutamate/) without allosteric inhibitors. The first high-resolution structure of the ion channel blocker-bound state was achieved using a DeltaATD construct (ATD removed), revealing the MK-801 and memantine binding sites at the M3 helix bundle crossing and M2 pore loop region (Song et al., 2018).

**Expression:**

- **Expression system**: X-ray structures: HEK293S GnTI- cells (suspension culture) with BacMam virus. [Cryo Em](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/structure-determination/cryo-em/) structures: Spodoptera frugiperda (Sf9) baculovirus system. Science 2014 structure: Sf9 insect cells with recombinant baculovirus using Drosophila melanogaster Hsp70 heat shock promoter (conventional late promoters P10 and polyhedrin hamper heteromeric assembly).

- **Construct**: X-ray: GluN1 (residues 1-834) and GluN2B (residues 1-839) from Xenopus laevis. DeltaATD GluN1 (residues 394-834) and DeltaATD GluN2B (residues 400-839). [Cryo Em](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/structure-determination/cryo-em/): Full-length rat GluN1b and GluN2B NMDA receptors. Science 2014: Modified GluN1-4a and GluN2B subunits (GluN1a-GluN2B_cryst) from Xenopus laevis. Disulfide cross-links engineered between subunits for stabilization.

**Expression:**

- **Expression system**: X-ray structures: HEK293S GnTI- cells (suspension culture) with BacMam virus. [Cryo Em](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/structure-determination/cryo-em/) structures: Spodoptera frugiperda (Sf9) baculovirus system. Science 2014 structure: Sf9 insect cells with recombinant baculovirus using Drosophila melanogaster Hsp70 heat shock promoter (conventional late promoters P10 and polyhedrin hamper heteromeric assembly).

- **Construct**: X-ray: GluN1 (residues 1-834) and GluN2B (residues 1-839) from Xenopus laevis. DeltaATD GluN1 (residues 394-834) and DeltaATD GluN2B (residues 400-839). [Cryo Em](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/structure-determination/cryo-em/): Full-length rat GluN1b and GluN2B NMDA receptors. Science 2014: Modified GluN1-4a and GluN2B subunits (GluN1a-GluN2B_cryst) from Xenopus laevis. Disulfide cross-links engineered between subunits for stabilization.

    </tr>

### doi/10.1038##s41586-018-0039-9

**Structures:**

<table class="wiki-table">
  <thead><tr>
    <th>PDB ID</th>
    <th>Resolution</th>
    <th>Space Group</th>
    <th>Construct</th>
    <th>Ligand/Co-factor</th>
  </tr></thead>
  <tbody>
    <tr>
      <td><a class="pdb-link" href="https://www.rcsb.org/structure/5un1">5UN1</a></td>
      <td>3.60</td>
      <td>C2</td>
      <td>DeltaATD GluN1/GluN2B NMDA receptor from Xenopus laevis. Residues 23-393 removed from GluN1, residues 1-399 removed from GluN2B. Human placental alkaline phosphatase signal sequence added to N-terminus of GluN2B. Thermostabilizing mutation G610R. Bound to <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/mk-801/">Mk 801</a>, <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/glycine/">Glycine</a>, and glutamate.
</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/mk-801/">Mk 801</a>, <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/glycine/">Glycine</a>, glutamate</td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>

**Expression:**

- **Expression system**: X-ray structures: HEK293S GnTI- cells (suspension culture) with BacMam virus. [Cryo Em](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/structure-determination/cryo-em/) structures: Spodoptera frugiperda (Sf9) baculovirus system. Science 2014 structure: Sf9 insect cells with recombinant baculovirus using Drosophila melanogaster Hsp70 heat shock promoter (conventional late promoters P10 and polyhedrin hamper heteromeric assembly).

- **Construct**: X-ray: GluN1 (residues 1-834) and GluN2B (residues 1-839) from Xenopus laevis. DeltaATD GluN1 (residues 394-834) and DeltaATD GluN2B (residues 400-839). [Cryo Em](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/structure-determination/cryo-em/): Full-length rat GluN1b and GluN2B NMDA receptors. Science 2014: Modified GluN1-4a and GluN2B subunits (GluN1a-GluN2B_cryst) from Xenopus laevis. Disulfide cross-links engineered between subunits for stabilization.


**Purification:**

<table class="wiki-table">
  <thead><tr>
    <th>Step</th>
    <th>Method</th>
    <th>Resin / Column</th>
    <th>Buffer + Detergent</th>
    <th>Notes</th>
  </tr></thead>
  <tbody>
    <tr>
      <td>Cell lysis and membrane preparation</td>
      <td>Sonication (4 <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/methods/purification/size-exclusion-chromatography/">SEC</a> on, 8 sec off for 10 min, power level 6.5)</td>
      <td>--</td>
      <td>150 mM NaCl, 20 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/tris/">Tris</a>(/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/tris/) pH 8.0 + --</td>
      <td>HEK293S GnTI- cells transduced with BacMam virus (MOI 1:1, GluN1:GluN2B). <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/additives/sodium-butyrate/">Sodium Butyrate</a> (10 mM) added at 14 hrs post-transduction, incubated at 30 C for 46 hrs. Cell debris removed at 6,000 x g; membranes collected at 125,000 x g.
</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>Membrane solubilization</td>
      <td>Stirring at 4 C for 2 hrs</td>
      <td>--</td>
      <td>150 mM NaCl, 20 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/tris/">Tris</a>(/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/tris/) pH 8.0, 0.8 mM aprotinin, 2 mg/ml leupeptin, 2 mM pepstatin A, 1 mM PMSF, 1 mM glutamate, 1 mM glycine + 1% <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/mng/">MNG-3</a>, 2 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/cholesterol-hydrogen-succinate/">CHS</a></td>
      <td>Insoluble material removed at 125,000 x g</td>
    </tr>

    </tr>

      <td>--</td>
      <td>400 mM NaCl, 20 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/mes/">MES</a> pH 6.5, 1 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/">DDM</a>, 0.2 mM CHS + 1 mM <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/detergents/ddm/">DDM</a>, 0.2 mM CHS</td>

    </tr>

### doi/10.1126##science.1251915

**Structures:**

<table class="wiki-table">
  <thead><tr>
    <th>PDB ID</th>
    <th>Resolution</th>
    <th>Space Group</th>
    <th>Construct</th>
    <th>Ligand/Co-factor</th>
  </tr></thead>
  <tbody>
    <tr>
      <td><a class="pdb-link" href="https://www.rcsb.org/structure/4pe5">4PE5</a></td>
      <td>5.70</td>
      <td>Not specified</td>
      <td>GluN1-4a and GluN2B subunits (GluN1a-GluN2B_cryst) expressed in Sf9 insect cells using baculovirus with Hsp70 promoter. Construct forms an ion channel activated by <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/glycine/">Glycine</a> and <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/substrates/l-glutamate/">L Glutamate</a>, allosterically regulated by ifenprodil and polyamines. Crystallized with glycine (GluN1 agonist), <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/substrates/l-glutamate/">L Glutamate</a> (GluN2 agonist), and ifenprodil (ATD-binding allosteric inhibitor). Structure solved by molecular replacement using extracellular domain probes. Later stabilized by disulfide cross-links between subunits for improved diffraction. Calcium binding site identified via holmium and gadolinium anomalous scattering.
</td>
      <td><a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/glycine/">Glycine</a>, <a href="/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/substrates/l-glutamate/">L Glutamate</a>, ifenprodil</td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>

**Expression:**

- **Expression system**: X-ray structures: HEK293S GnTI- cells (suspension culture) with BacMam virus. [Cryo Em](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/structure-determination/cryo-em/) structures: Spodoptera frugiperda (Sf9) baculovirus system. Science 2014 structure: Sf9 insect cells with recombinant baculovirus using Drosophila melanogaster Hsp70 heat shock promoter (conventional late promoters P10 and polyhedrin hamper heteromeric assembly).

- **Construct**: X-ray: GluN1 (residues 1-834) and GluN2B (residues 1-839) from Xenopus laevis. DeltaATD GluN1 (residues 394-834) and DeltaATD GluN2B (residues 400-839). [Cryo Em](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/structure-determination/cryo-em/): Full-length rat GluN1b and GluN2B NMDA receptors. Science 2014: Modified GluN1-4a and GluN2B subunits (GluN1a-GluN2B_cryst) from Xenopus laevis. Disulfide cross-links engineered between subunits for stabilization.

## Biological / Functional Insights

### ATD opening drives receptor activation

Upon agonist binding ([Glycine](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/glycine/) and [L Glutamate](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/substrates/l-glutamate/)) in the absence of ifenprodil, the GluN2B ATD opens by 14-21 degrees, increasing the distance between the two GluN1 ATDs by up to 29 Angstroms compared to the ifenprodil-bound inhibited state. The active conformation shows the ATD opening by approximately 22 degrees and rotation of GluN1b-GluN2B heterodimeric pairs by 12 degrees, strikingly similar to the apo-GluN1b-GluN2B ATD crystal structure.

### LBD rotation causes gating ring dilation

Transition from non-active to active conformation involves 13.5 degree rotation of GluN1b-GluN2B LBD heterodimers. This movement causes vertical displacement of GluN1b Arg684 and lateral separation of GluN2B Glu658 by 7 and 11 Angstroms respectively at the LBD-TMD linkers, dilating the gating ring formed by M3 helices of the transmembrane domain.

### Three distinct conformational states

3D classification of [Cryo Em](/xray-mp-wiki/methods/structure-determination/cryo-em/) data reveals three distinct conformations: non-active1, non-active2, and active. Both non-active states have agonists bound to LBD but closed ion channels. Non-active2 has a 7 degree more open GluN2B ATD than non-active1, resulting in 13 Angstrom larger separation between GluN1 ATDs.

### MK-801 binds in the channel vestibule between M3 bundle crossing and M2 pore loops

The 3.6 A crystal structure of the DeltaATD NMDA receptor (PDB 5UN1) reveals that [Mk 801](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/mk-801/) resides within the ion channel vestibule, with its nitrogen atom near N612 (GluN2B). The two aromatic rings of [Mk 801](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/mk-801/) are juxtaposed next to the M3 helix of the GluN1 subunit near V642 (GluN1), while the methyl substituent is near L640 on the M3 helix (GluN2B). Substitutions of GluN1 V642A, V642L and GluN2B L640A extinguish [Mk 801](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/mk-801/) binding.

### MK-801 and memantine block by physical occlusion and gate closure

Long-timescale MD simulations (aggregate ~900 microseconds) show that both [Mk 801](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/mk-801/) and [Memantine](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/memantine/) bind within the TMD vestibule along the ion permeation pathway and promote closure of the ion channel gate at the M3 bundle-crossing region via hydrophobic collapse. MK-801 binds in two 2-fold related poses while [Memantine](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/memantine/) binds in a single predominant pose. The calculated Kd values are approximately 0.08 microM for MK-801 and 7.6 microM for [Memantine](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/memantine/), showing a ~100-fold relative affinity difference consistent with experimental values.

### Lipid tunnels connect the central vestibule to the membrane bilayer

Near the M2 helices of the TMD, two tunnels connect the central vestibule to the interior of the membrane bilayer. The tunnels pass through cavities between the GluN1 M2 and M3 helices and adjacent GluN2B M3 helices, with radii ranging from 1.3-2.9 A, large enough to accommodate aliphatic tails of lipids. MD simulations show lipid tails transiently entering these tunnels.

### Hot-air balloon architecture with compact ATD-LBD packing

The GluN1a-GluN2B NMDA receptor bound to [Glycine](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/buffers/glycine/), [L Glutamate](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/substrates/l-glutamate/), and ifenprodil adopts a hot-air balloon shape where the extracellular domains form the balloon and the TMD forms the basket. Unlike the Y-shaped GluA2 AMPA receptor, the NMDA receptor shows tight packing between the ATD and LBD layers, attributed to extensive intersubunit interactions. The ATD-LBD interface involves upper lobes of GluN1a subunits and lower lobes of GluN2B subunits, forming two interfaces between heterodimers - a more compact arrangement than the single interface in GluA2 AMPA receptors.

### Domain swapping between ATD and LBD layers determines 1-2-1-2 arrangement

The NMDA receptor subunits assemble in a staggered GluN1-GluN2-GluN1-GluN2 (1-2-1-2) heterotetrameric arrangement. Domain swapping occurs between ATD and LBD layers: ATD heterodimer pairs assemble as GluN1a(alpha)-GluN2B(alpha) and GluN1(beta)-GluN2B(beta), while LBD pairs swap to GluN1a(alpha)-GluN2B(beta) and GluN1(beta)-GluN2B(alpha). The LBD interfaces favor this arrangement through steric compatibility - GluN1a-GluN1a interactions are blocked by collisions between loop1 and helix G, while GluN2B-GluN2B interactions are disfavored by steric hindrance between helix K' and helices E'/F'.

### Calcium pooling at the extracellular vestibule via DRPEER motif

The DRPEER motif (acidic residues in GluN1 located at the LBD-TMD linkers) creates a calcium pool just outside the ion channel pore. Lanthanide binding sites (holmium, gadolinium) identified at the extracellular vestibule over the M3 helix bundle confirm this charge-based ion pooling mechanism, similar to that proposed for P2X4 receptors and nicotinic [Acetylcholine](/xray-mp-wiki/reagents/ligands/acetylcholine/) receptors. This calcium pool is critical for the high Ca2+ flux characteristic of NMDA receptors and contributes to neuronal plasticity and excitotoxicity.

### M3 helix gating mechanics resemble KcsA potassium channel

The ion channel pore (M1-M3) of the GluN1a-GluN2B NMDA receptor shows high structural similarity to [Kcsa](/xray-mp-wiki/proteins/voltage-gated-channels/kcsa/) potassium channels in the closed conformation (RMSD 2.4 A), despite only 19% sequence identity. The M3 helices cross at the highly conserved SYTANIAAF motif, occluding the ion penetration pathway in the allosterically inhibited state. In contrast, open K+ channels (Shaker, MthK) do not superpose well, suggesting gating of the NMDA receptor may involve rearrangement of M3 helices similar to potassium channel gating.
